  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_52220d21-c4f3-40c1-bbbb-d412c15773e3'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText10263089468682327699" style="display:none">Angels are all around us: beautiful, awe-inspiring, irresistible.<br /><br />Ordinary mortals yearn to catch a glimpse of one of these stunning beings and thousands flock to The Church of Angels to feel their healing touch.<br />But what if their potent magnetism isn't what it seems?<br />Willow knows she's different from other girls. And not just because she loves tinkering around with cars.<br />Willow has a gift. She can look into people's futures, know their dreams, their hopes and their regrets, just by touching them. But she has no idea where she gets this power from.<br /><br />Until she meets Alex…<br />Alex is one of the few who know the truth about angels. He knows Willow's secret and is on a mission to stop her.<br />The dark forces within Willow make her dangerous – and irresistible.<br />In spite of himself, Alex finds he is falling in love with his sworn enemy.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11779050542654348333"><a href='http://media.photobucket.com/image/bollywood%20sign/c_cinema/Bollywood_Sign.jpg?o=0' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700000._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Bollywood has a special genre of movies called 'Masala movies'. Masala, in case you're wondering, is a powdered mixture of spices to add flavour to Indian cuisine. Masala movies, on the same note, are a mixture of dramatic elements designed to appeal to the senses. <br/><br/><b>STEP 1: Boy Meets Girl</b><br/><br/><a href='http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/cherry_blossom_88/kareena%20kapoor/jab%20we%20met/1222.gif?o=4' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700001.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Boy and girl bump into each other/ meet at a wedding/ are introduced by friends and there is an instant 'connection' which will, of course, soon lead to true lurrve. <br/><br/><b>STEP 2: Girl Plays Coy</b><br/><br/><a href='http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/cherry_blossom_88/kareena%20kapoor/jab%20we%20met/4m7d75z.jpg?o=9' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700002.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The path of </span>
  <span id="freeText11779050542654348333" style="display:none"><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/bollywood%20sign/c_cinema/Bollywood_Sign.jpg?o=0" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700000._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Bollywood has a special genre of movies called 'Masala movies'. Masala, in case you're wondering, is a powdered mixture of spices to add flavour to Indian cuisine. Masala movies, on the same note, are a mixture of dramatic elements designed to appeal to the senses. <br><br><b>STEP 1: Boy Meets Girl</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/cherry_blossom_88/kareena%20kapoor/jab%20we%20met/1222.gif?o=4" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700001.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Boy and girl bump into each other/ meet at a wedding/ are introduced by friends and there is an instant 'connection' which will, of course, soon lead to true lurrve. <br><br><b>STEP 2: Girl Plays Coy</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/cherry_blossom_88/kareena%20kapoor/jab%20we%20met/4m7d75z.jpg?o=9" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700002.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The path of true lurrve is never smooth, so of course, our hero and/or heroine hate each other on sight. Our heroine fight with, teases, yet secretly dreams of her annoying yet adorable hero. <br><br><b>STEP 3: Discovering Love through Song</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/aishwarya_06/mauja3ah1.gif?o=38" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345320ra/700003.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What good is a Bollywood movie without a song?!! <br><br><b>STEP 4: Enter Bad Guy</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/gabbar%20sholay/simmi02/7.jpg?o=0" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700004.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Star-crossed lovers need a reason to be star-crossed, right? Cue Bad Guy. The role of the bad guy is simple: Look ugly, act threatening, kidnap and/or threaten to kill heroine.<br><br><b>STEP 5: Dramatic Separation</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/cherry_blossom_88/kareena%20kapoor/jab%20we%20met/486w9z9.jpg?o=8" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700005.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Of course, since the heroine must face the death at the hands of the bad guy, it is her duty to face her fate bravely, and just as bravely entreat the hero to save himself and not some after her (<i>subtext: if you don't come after me, you bastard, I'll rise from the grave and cut your balls off</i>). Since every hero has an ardent desire to <s>save his genitalia</s> save his true lurrve, the hero will, of course, ignore this brave advice and run boldly after the heroine. While he does so, of course, there will be a flashback of all his tender memories of the heroine, and a song. <br><br><b>STEP 5.1: Song of Remembrance</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/aishwarya_06/mauja2rd6.gif?o=37" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345320ra/700006.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>STEP 6: Hero Saves the Day</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/shahid%20kapoor/TuJaaneNa/Shahid%20Kapoor/shahid-clinicallclear.jpg?o=17" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700007._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Arriving in the nick of time, the Hero bravely battles the bad guy while the heroine has swooned from her efforts to protect her chastity. Emerging the victor, it is time for the hero to do a victory dance. <br><br><b>STEP 6.1: Victory Song</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/shahid%20kapoor/zxcvbnm41/sahil%20khan/shahid-kapoor.jpg?o=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <span>[image error]</span>
</a><br><br><br><b>STEP 7: Happily Ever After (Song)</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/cherry_blossom_88/kareena%20kapoor/jab%20we%20met/4u146f9.jpg?o=10" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700009.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Our Hero and Heroine get married and live happily ever after. <br><br><b>STEP 7.1: Riding off into the Sunset (Song)</b><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/kareena%20jab%20we%20met/cherry_blossom_88/kareena%20kapoor/jab%20we%20met/5871834c6c2bdf64832e9b3dc4b2119bec3.jpg?o=14" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380345320i/700010.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ah, eco-friendly true love! <br><br><br>Now, on to the review:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9713071.Angel_Burn" title="Angel Burn by L.A. Weatherly" rel="nofollow noopener">Angel Burn</a> would make SUCH a FABULOUS masala movie! I think I'll go tell <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karan_Johar" rel="nofollow noopener">Karan Johar</a> to option the movie rights to this book right now! <br><br>P.S. I received a copy of this book from the publishers via Net Galley. No monetary or other considerations affected my review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11779050542654348333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_239188803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239188803" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239188803?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763656522" href="/book/show/9713071-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239188803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer783056036600269764"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I realise it was probably a mistake to read another angel book so soon after finishing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_' title='Angelfall (Penryn & the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angelfall</a>, but it was amongst the gushing reviews and comments on the aforementioned that I read about these two books sharing a similar theme. This theme being that, rather than having pretty, sparkly, heaven-sent angels, the authors used the more traditional, violent creatures who have come to earth in order to take over. However, this is where the similarities between the two novels end.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9713071.Angel_Burn' title='Angel Burn by L.A. Weatherly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angel Burn</a> has a</span>
  <span id="freeText783056036600269764" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I realise it was probably a mistake to read another angel book so soon after finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>, but it was amongst the gushing reviews and comments on the aforementioned that I read about these two books sharing a similar theme. This theme being that, rather than having pretty, sparkly, heaven-sent angels, the authors used the more traditional, violent creatures who have come to earth in order to take over. However, this is where the similarities between the two novels end.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9713071.Angel_Burn" title="Angel Burn by L.A. Weatherly" rel="nofollow noopener">Angel Burn</a> has a much heavier focus on romance. In fact, the majority of the book is taken up by the development of the relationship between the male and female protagonists who are, of course, drawn to each other from the very beginning. I cannot help but be annoyed when the heroine pauses in life-threatening situtations to ogle this novel's piece of man candy. Is this normal behaviour? Surely myself and Penryn cannot be the only ones to prefer survival?<br><br>Naturally, they are already eternally, unconditionally in love by the novel's half-way marker. I also would guess that the equivalent of about sixty pages in total is given to Willow and Alex's kissing sessions. Way too much of this rather large book was about the romance. And what was the plot, exactly?<br><br>Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10677277.Article_5__Article_5___1_" title="Article 5 (Article 5, #1) by Kristen Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">Article 5</a>, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9554790.The_Other_Life__The_Other_Life___1_" title="The Other Life (The Other Life, #1) by Susanne Winnacker" rel="nofollow noopener">The Other Life</a>, the bad guys are not actually that important. They are merely the tool needed to get the two lovebirds on the run together and allow for the road trip romancing to take place. Unlike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>, the angel mythology is so underdeveloped. This could quite easily have been a book about vampires, werewolves, aliens - take your pick. You'd only have to change a few words and phrases here and there.<br><br>Perhaps it would not have been so bad if the romance hadn't been so damn corny as well. I'm not totally immune to the charms of a sexy guy in a leather jacket and the call of a touching romance, but this pulled some scenes that I'm pretty sure only Disney can get away with. You know what I mean, one of them is lying on the ground and <i>no, please no, you can't be dead... I love you</i> and then their eyes flicker open! Oh, please.<br><br>If you're a hardcore PNR fan or haven't already read way too much annoying paranormal novels then this could be for you. If you've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a> recently, though, I recommend waiting a good while before reading this because, in my opinion, it pales in comparison.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="783056036600269764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_156344316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156344316" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156344316?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763656522" href="/book/show/9713071-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-angels">pn-angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=favorite-ya">favorite-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2011-favorites">2011-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2011-publication">2011-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=crush-worthy-boys">crush-worthy-boys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156344316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8755082770662157996"><b>Free for Kindle right now!</b> <a href='http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B004UI6E6W' rel='nofollow noopener'>Download from Amazon</a> before the deal ends. (Review edited 6/3/11 to include this freebie.)<br/><br/>There's something a-brew in the heavens, because there has been a streak of great books centered around angels lately. After disappointments like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_' title='Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hush, Hush</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_' title='Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fallen</a>, and various other novels, it's exciting to have books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_' title='Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unearthly</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8373527.Mercy__Mercy___1_' title='Mercy (Mercy, #1) by Rebecca Lim' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mercy</a> ...and now Angel Burn, which is the first in a trilogy previously published in the U.K. under a slightly different title.<br/><br/>What's unusual ab</span>
  <span id="freeText8755082770662157996" style="display:none"><b>Free for Kindle right now!</b> <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B004UI6E6W" rel="nofollow noopener">Download from Amazon</a> before the deal ends. (Review edited 6/3/11 to include this freebie.)<br /><br />There's something a-brew in the heavens, because there has been a streak of great books centered around angels lately. After disappointments like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_" title="Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush, Hush</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_" title="Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen</a>, and various other novels, it's exciting to have books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8373527.Mercy__Mercy___1_" title="Mercy (Mercy, #1) by Rebecca Lim" rel="nofollow noopener">Mercy</a> ...and now Angel Burn, which is the first in a trilogy previously published in the U.K. under a slightly different title.<br /><br />What's unusual about this book is that it takes the whole notion of angels as kindly guardians and turns it upside down. Angels want something very badly from humans in this story, and their secret is a pretty devastating one. Willow is a clairvoyant who sees flashes of the future for anyone she touches, and is horrified by a disturbing vision she sees while doing a reading for a classmate. In the meantime, alternate chapters follow a sexy and mysterious young assassin named Alex, who first sees Willow as a nemesis, but who gradually helps her to uncover incredible secrets about her past--and about her future.<br /><br />Willow and Alex are both fantastic characters on their own, making mature decisions and doing their best in an impossible situation, but they become stronger and even more appealing together. Throughout most of the book, they are on the run and alone in the car, so it's a testament to the writer that the reader remains engrossed in the mounting tension of the story as well as the slow burn of a relationship between the unlikely pair. Willow and Alex are deeply connected and funny and honest, and it's refreshing to read about a boy and a girl who are actually <i>nice</i> to each other, even when they have every compelling reason not to be. Angel Burn is a terrific page-turner with unforgettable characters, and readers will be on the edge of their seats waiting its sequels.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2011/04/angel-burn-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8755082770662157996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/12542477-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=ok-fine-its-ya">ok-fine-its-ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=ok-i-cheated">ok-i-cheated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327078-k?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi-dys">fantasy-sci-fi-dys</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286325615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10186711366594177466">So, my thoughts during and after reading <i>Angel Burn</i>:<br/><br/>Ahem...<br/><br/>- Weatherly is not a bad writer. Truly, she isn't. But I felt like this book lacked epicness and research. It was a small world trying to seem big. A small war trying to seem all-ending. I felt like she sat down and used up any standing information she had about angel lore and, somehow, managed to compose an entire novel. What she should've done was spend a little more time in the library (or the internet, don't be scared) to give us mor</span>
  <span id="freeText10186711366594177466" style="display:none">So, my thoughts during and after reading <i>Angel Burn</i>:<br /><br />Ahem...<br /><br />- Weatherly is not a bad writer. Truly, she isn't. But I felt like this book lacked epicness and research. It was a small world trying to seem big. A small war trying to seem all-ending. I felt like she sat down and used up any standing information she had about angel lore and, somehow, managed to compose an entire novel. What she should've done was spend a little more time in the library (or the internet, don't be scared) to give us more depth.<br /><br />- This was cheesy as fck. "Project Angel"? Angel Killers? (Omigod, okay so this one, I was like <i>"watch AK stand for Angel Killers, haha! That would be the biggest, most hilarious fail, hah--oh"</i>) Angel Burn? Chakra Points? Willow knowing hot things about cars? The fcking C.I.A.? <br /><br />- Willow and Alex <i>really</i> liked to talk about how much they love each other. Like, over and over again. <br /><br />- Too many p.o.v.s. There's no element of surprise when we know everything that's coming around the corner. Bad move.<br /><br />There were good things, too. <br /><br />But I don't remember them. </span>

<div id="review_142665413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142665413" />
    <a title="Fani *loves angst*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1133802-fani-loves-angst"><img alt="Fani *loves angst*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398440418p2/1133802.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142665413?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fani *loves angst*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fani *loves angst*" href="/user/show/1133802-fani-loves-angst">Fani *loves angst*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763656522" href="/book/show/9713071-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=arc-netgalley">arc-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=romance-pnr">romance-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=assassin-mercenary">assassin-mercenary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1133802-fani-loves-angst?shelf=lethal-hero">lethal-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142665413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10197437048082298240">Simply put, I think this is the best young adult paranormal book I've read (though admittedly my knowledge in the genre is rather limited). But whereas YA books usually bore me with the endless descriptions of everyday high school life, this one took a different approach, much more to my liking: that of a road-trip.<br/><br/>Willow has always been psychic and has the ability to see glimpses of the future. One day while reading a girl's thoughts she sees a real angel. Surprisingly though, the angel seems t</span>
  <span id="freeText10197437048082298240" style="display:none">Simply put, I think this is the best young adult paranormal book I've read (though admittedly my knowledge in the genre is rather limited). But whereas YA books usually bore me with the endless descriptions of everyday high school life, this one took a different approach, much more to my liking: that of a road-trip.<br /><br />Willow has always been psychic and has the ability to see glimpses of the future. One day while reading a girl's thoughts she sees a real angel. Surprisingly though, the angel seems to be hurting her friend rather than helping her and Willow tries in vain to stop Heather from joining the newfound Church of the Angels. When Willow herself goes to the Church for a last attempt to stop Heather she sees more angels feeding off humans, leaving them drained and weak. <br />Unbeknownst to Willow, the angels have been notified of her existence and consider her a threat. For this reason, they send someone to kill her; someone who's in fact an Angel Killer. When Alex, who's the assassin, meets Willow, he realizes that something is very wrong with this mission and decides to watch her a while before actually killing her. So he follows her to the Church of the Angels only to see the Angels attacking her. And since 'my enemy's enemy is my friend' as the old adage goes, he decides to save Willow until he knows why the Angels want her dead. Thus, they both get into his car and their road trip begins.<br /><br />For one, there is no way that this book is going to bore you. The action and suspense is non-stop till the very end, while the on-the-road element added much to my enjoyment. These two constantly meet new people, visit new places and in between they get closer to each other. Thus when they finally admit to their attraction, I could actually believe it, since they were not strangers at that point. <br /><br />I liked the writing, simple and to the point but with some beautiful descriptions of the desert and later the mountains that made me feel as if I was actually there. I liked the characters too; both calm, composed Willow and lonely, decisive Alex. Although they were only 17 and 18 years old respectively, they both acted maturely like adults, which was very understandable and realistic considering their childhoods.<br /><br />If -like me- you read only a couple of YA books per year, make this one of them. It's definitely worth your time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10197437048082298240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115080900" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115080900" />
    <a title="Nic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2813423-nic"><img alt="Nic" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115080900?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nic" href="/user/show/2813423-nic">Nic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=angels">angels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115080900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2365431874739321823"><b>Favourite Quote:</b> <i>"It' worth it you know," said Alex, smiling into my eyes. "What is?" I said. His thumb moved slowly over my cheek. "All of this. Having you. It's worth - anything."</i><br/><br/>I have found another awesome angel book. Last year it seemed I was having the worst run with angel themed books. They were all a little too similar and I was thinking maybe they weren't for me. But Angel is nothing like any other angel book I have read before. Not only does it have a unique concept but has great blend</span>
  <span id="freeText2365431874739321823" style="display:none"><b>Favourite Quote:</b> <i>"It' worth it you know," said Alex, smiling into my eyes. "What is?" I said. His thumb moved slowly over my cheek. "All of this. Having you. It's worth - anything."</i><br /><br />I have found another awesome angel book. Last year it seemed I was having the worst run with angel themed books. They were all a little too similar and I was thinking maybe they weren't for me. But Angel is nothing like any other angel book I have read before. Not only does it have a unique concept but has great blend of heart pumping action, surprising twists and turns and a captivating romance.<br /><br />First off the mythology is really something that makes this book standout from the rest. Angels feed off humans causing them death, insanity and disease and it is called angel burn. And most people can't see it as they are too blinded by the angel's beauty. The mythology though is easy to understand and comes together well as the story is explained and is quite interesting.<br /><br />Angel alternates from both Willow's and Alex's points of views and smoothly changes from one to the other. Also every now and then you get a point of view from two of the secondary characters that play an important part in the story. The pace is mostly quick and engaging. There are couple of slow points in the book but it is 500 pages long and overall held my interest the whole way through.<br /><br />The characterization was good. Willow is a little different from the average girl with her psychic abilities and love of cars. She is instantly likeable. Alex is the dark, sexy, mysterious type and completely crush worthy. Their romance builds slowly at first but then turns into that epic type of love. Very mushy but in a good way.<br /><br />Overall, this was fantastic start to this trilogy and I can't wait for more!<br /><br /><b>Bookers Warning</b>: Some of you lovely ladies at SCB may find the romance in this book too mushy for your taste. </span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3603005-amber?shelf=arc">arc</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133554042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5422047684540867191">This brilliant, action packed page turner will have you on the edge of your seat craving for more!! This is a MUST READ for 2011!!!<br/><br/>This story is about a girl named Willow, who isn’t the typical high school student from Pawtucket, a sleepy little town crouched in the foothills of the Adirondack Mountains. Willow has always been able to read people by touching them and by doing so she can see into their future. <br/><br/>The story starts off with a classmate of Willow’s wanting a reading. Willow was feeling</span>
  <span id="freeText5422047684540867191" style="display:none">This brilliant, action packed page turner will have you on the edge of your seat craving for more!! This is a MUST READ for 2011!!!<br /><br />This story is about a girl named Willow, who isn’t the typical high school student from Pawtucket, a sleepy little town crouched in the foothills of the Adirondack Mountains. Willow has always been able to read people by touching them and by doing so she can see into their future. <br /><br />The story starts off with a classmate of Willow’s wanting a reading. Willow was feeling a little apprehensive because she had a bad feeling about it. This is when the story really starts to evolve and the characters start to emerge. <br /><br />L.A. Weatherly executed the timing just right when she introduced the beautiful and cunning assassin Alex. He’s quick on his feet and fighting for a purpose but when he is sent on a mission to terminate Willow, he has a change of heart and upon watching her in the shadows, he finds her to be beautiful. <br /><br />The story takes off quickly from this point and doesn’t stop until the very end when the page is blank and you are thirsting for more. I loved the action and adventure in this book. All I can say is that you yourself will have to read this for yourself. This will be added to my favorites of 2011.<br /><br />Thank you Candlewick Press and NetGalley for this AMAZING read!!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238175378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9661873269380102718"><u>Angel Burn</u> by L.A. Weatherly<br/><br/>First in the Angel Trilogy<br/><br/><b>5 stars</b><br/><br/><p>Willow has always known she was different from other girls and just because she’s a pro at fixing cars. Willow can see the future and know people’s dreams, hopes, regrets, and their paths that can be taken just by touching them. She doesn’t know where this power came from. Alex, an assassin, knows. Alex isn’t just any assassin he’s an AK (Angel Assassin). Angels aren’t heavenly beings they suck out human energy leaving cancer, mental i</p></span>
  <span id="freeText9661873269380102718" style="display:none"><u>Angel Burn</u> by L.A. Weatherly<br><br>First in the Angel Trilogy<br><br><b>5 stars</b><br><br><p>Willow has always known she was different from other girls and just because she’s a pro at fixing cars. Willow can see the future and know people’s dreams, hopes, regrets, and their paths that can be taken just by touching them. She doesn’t know where this power came from. Alex, an assassin, knows. Alex isn’t just any assassin he’s an AK (Angel Assassin). Angels aren’t heavenly beings they suck out human energy leaving cancer, mental illnesses, and other diseases in their wake. Willow is a half-angel. Something that isn’t supposed to be possible and now Willow and Alex are on the run. When Alex finds himself falling for Willow he starts to see that not everything is black and white. This book was amazing. Pure, absolute awesomeness and I’m just dumbfounded. Even though this book was somewhat predictable I wasn’t expecting the ending and I need more now. The plot was fantastic and the whole concept of angels being evil completely new and fresh. I loved it. Being introduced to new ideas like this is what makes reading so enjoyable. The writing was a little hard for me to adjust to, but I have the same problem I pick up a J.R. Ward novel, but I usually absolutely love her works and I loved Angel Burn it was just fantastic. Really the only thing that bothered me was the writing at first after that there was no problems for me. I thought this book was perfect and I loved it.</p><br><br><b>Whimsical Writing Scale: 5</b><br><br><p>The main female character is Willow. Willow is a great heroine. She has a backbone and when Alex was being a jerk she didn’t let him push her around like some heroines in YA would. I respect her struggle with her coming to terms with the fact that she’s half-angel. Willow was just a good YA heroine and I can’t think of very many faults and the ones I can think of aren’t worth mentioning.</p><br><br><b>Kick-Butt Heroine Scale: 4.75</b><br><br><p>The main male character is Alex. Yes he was a jerk to Willow, but since we got POVS from Alex’s POV I understood why he pushed her away. I like Alex. No, I’ve come to love Alex. He’s very protective of Willow and I can’t wait to see where their relationship goes.</p><br><br><b>Swoon Worthy Scale: 4.75</b><br><br><p><b>The Villain</b>- The Angels, but if we want a specific villain let’s say Raziel. Raziel is the ringleader of the angels and he has a strong hold over humans and angels.</p><br><br><b>Villain Scale: 4</b><br><br><p>Jonah was another POV. I liked Jonah and I have a feeling he’s going to be a big help in defeating the angels in the next books. I like Jonah, but I hope he doesn’t become a love interest for Willow. I highly doubt he will, but I don’t want a love triangle.</p><br><br><b>Character Scale: 4.75</b><br><br><p>I’m happy to inform there was no insta-love. There was a connection, but for a while they ignored each other and Willow was mad at him (I don’t blame her), but their hate turned to love then friendship then love. I didn’t think it was rushed. They spent so much time together I would’ve been shocked if they hadn’t developed feelings for one another. I’m so glad I picked this book up at my library. I can’t wait to read Angel Fire. My expectations are high and I’m going book hunting. Hopefully my library has Angel Fire. Angel Fire I need you...<br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/i%20need%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363567ra/714987.gif" alt="i need gif Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></p><br><br><b>Plotastic Scale: 5</b><br><br><b>Cover Thoughts: I like the cover. The girl looks like she’s standing next to a fire and it’s captivating, but my favorite part of the cover has to be the little design around the title. If you’ve seen the cover in person you’ll know what I’m talking about.</b><br><br>Other Reviews in This Trilogy:<br>2) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372714579" rel="nofollow noopener">Angel Fire</a> <b>4 stars</b><br>3) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372714632" rel="nofollow noopener">Angel Fever</a> <b>2.25 stars</b></span>

<div id="review_139822860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139822860" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320017147p2/4515165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139822860?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763656522" href="/book/show/9713071-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139822860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13255698653746593974">My bar for ranking new angel books is admittedly low--I mean, look at the comps and see the lack of competition. Until Unearthly, I was beginning to think it may be impossible to write a decent angel book. Out of all paranormal creatures, angels have received the worse treatment in YA books BY FAR. I won't go into the examples--we all know what they are.<br/><br/>With Angel Burn, I was pleasantly surprised. The wearisome elements plaguing other angel books (TSTL heroines, creepy obsessive love interests, </span>
  <span id="freeText13255698653746593974" style="display:none">My bar for ranking new angel books is admittedly low--I mean, look at the comps and see the lack of competition. Until Unearthly, I was beginning to think it may be impossible to write a decent angel book. Out of all paranormal creatures, angels have received the worse treatment in YA books BY FAR. I won't go into the examples--we all know what they are.<br /><br />With Angel Burn, I was pleasantly surprised. The wearisome elements plaguing other angel books (TSTL heroines, creepy obsessive love interests, shoddy mythology) were largely absent. Both Willow and Alex are unique and likeable. While they are immediately attracted to each other, the actual romance builds for much of the book, and the insta-love is kept to a happy minimum. Yes, it was the hunter-falling-in-love-with-his-prey we've seen done before, but the chemistry between Willow and Alex and the way the author let the attraction simmer for chapter after chapter had me hooked.<br /><br />Although Angel Burn has a slow start, the pacing picks up immediately once Willow and Alex begin their road-trip escape. The story does descend into gooey teenage love about 2/3 of the way in, but at least the author let Willow and Alex spend time together and get to know each other first.<br /><br />While I'm not sure why these creatures are called angels (they're certainly not angelic in the traditional sense and don't seem to come from Heaven) they were the perfect villains--sufficiently creepy and evil. The mythology is developed enough to make sense, and it's definitely unique.<br /><br />I'm happy to say that with its original mythology, likeable main characters, and simmering romance, Angel Burn far surpasses many of its angel book competitors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13255698653746593974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_114369362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114369362?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763656522" href="/book/show/9713071-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114369362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1758680828368908410">TBR Reduce Challenge #15- 2011 (Stefanie) <br/><br/>I've read a lot of Angel books and sometimes I find ones that has a different take on the traditional lore. But, <b>Angel</b> is probably the most unique of them all, and while I'm not use to seeing angels as the bad guys, being hunted, I still think this was an excellent concept. Mix it with suspense, grip and forbidden love and how could I resist?<br/><br/>Fresh, smart and fantastic! Can't wait to read the next book; <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9553503.Angel_Fire__Angel_Trilogy___2_' title='Angel Fire (Angel Trilogy, #2) by L.A. Weatherly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angel Fire</a>!</span>
  <span id="freeText1758680828368908410" style="display:none">TBR Reduce Challenge #15- 2011 (Stefanie) <br /><br />I've read a lot of Angel books and sometimes I find ones that has a different take on the traditional lore. But, <b>Angel</b> is probably the most unique of them all, and while I'm not use to seeing angels as the bad guys, being hunted, I still think this was an excellent concept. Mix it with suspense, grip and forbidden love and how could I resist?<br /><br />Fresh, smart and fantastic! Can't wait to read the next book; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9553503.Angel_Fire__Angel_Trilogy___2_" title="Angel Fire (Angel Trilogy, #2) by L.A. Weatherly" rel="nofollow noopener">Angel Fire</a>!</span>

  <span id="freeText2645912845747942621" style="display:none"><b> 14/01/2013 </b> Proud owner of the audiobook as well! <br /><br /><br />I was waiting for this book months and the moment i grap it i have no idea what happend and i held back on reading it at least 2 weeks!I wish i wouldnt done it to be honest because simply i was thrilled with the book!<br /><br />Yes you may heard right that the book is for an angel and it might sound to you similiar with some other book you might read recently!But i personally enjoy it and in fact i finished in 3 nights ending with red eyes without proper sleep!<br /><br />I have to say that Alex and Willow is a great couple.. and when i mean a great couple i really mean it!I like that that they started completely hating each other but slowly and slowly getting to know each other and to fall in love with other (not out of the blue like in some other books goes)<br /><br />I pretty much like Willow the character how she become in love with Alex but the basic thing is i Loved how strong and confident she was when she had to do ... what she had to do anyway ;) even that she scared and all of these things! <br /><br />Alex is/was lovely!I felt so sympathy with him how his past was how he had to deal with the situation with his family and all!And i gotta say i really like how He as well become in love with Willow at the same time she did as well!<br /><br />Writing was good and you may comfuse a bit in the start because the POV of things switch back and forth from Willow and Alex and other characters too (''bad'' as well)but you get used of it eventually and i dare to say i even like it too! <br /><br />The basic thing i was thrilled in a way with this book is because the romance and the action is switch on and off i mean one chapter there is the development between Alex and Willow and all then there is the action happening! I pretty much like how those 2 stuff was on and off without you getting bored and having all the suspense whats going on what is going to happend keep you continue reading it even that they actually start ruuning from the first chapters!<br /><br />What i didnt like?Well i was very dissapointed how the dark/evil side of Angels describe...OK we know they are bad and they using humans and all BUT the describion was more like...I just wasnt able to picture it they way it did in the book! I felt more like a shapeshifter with wings was on rather than an Angel with bad purpose and all of this stuff! <br /><br />Overall i like it and i am waiting for the second book!</span>

<div id="review_128204407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128204407" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128204407?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763656522" href="/book/show/9713071-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128204407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer144754949496129354">I bought this book from the Book Depo, since it's been released in the UK for several months now, but I didn't actually read the story until I had a copy of the US galley in hand. I'm not sure why I waited so long, my fellow UK bloggers had all but demanded that I read this book! I am a fan of the US cover over the UK one though! Though they both are beautiful.<br/><br/>Angel Burn is unlike any angel themed story I've read. When I think of angels I think of goodness and white lights... healing touches, ya</span>
  <span id="freeText144754949496129354" style="display:none">I bought this book from the Book Depo, since it's been released in the UK for several months now, but I didn't actually read the story until I had a copy of the US galley in hand. I'm not sure why I waited so long, my fellow UK bloggers had all but demanded that I read this book! I am a fan of the US cover over the UK one though! Though they both are beautiful.<br /><br />Angel Burn is unlike any angel themed story I've read. When I think of angels I think of goodness and white lights... healing touches, yada yada. That's isn't the case for Weatherly's angels.<br /><br />The angels in Angel Burn, are for lack of a better word... straight up EVIL! They (well almost all of them) feed on humans. Drinking their very essence of life. Yet the humans they feed from are left with thoughts of elation. These angels have touched their lives in the most positive way. Yeah, that's messed up!<br /><br />Cue Alex, who is an AK. Yes, an angel KILLER! He is one of the few people that can see the angels doing their dirty work, and it's his personal mission to kill every last one of them. Too bad he ends up falling for one of them.... well a half one of them anyway, cue Willow.<br /><br />Alex and Willow, loved them. They were both great characters individually and separately. They balanced each other out very nicely. Although their romance had me gagging at it's sweetness in certain aspects, the sugar fiend in me ate it up.<br /><br />The story is told in multiple POVs which is something that I love! But I found myself getting a little confused with the change in narration... first person, third person... I got the hang of it after a while though.<br /><br />The ending was a little abrupt, I felt like we were leading up to this big showdown... and for me it was a little bang and sizzle... instead of bang and EXPLOSION! Really looking forward to seeing where the rest of the story goes. I will be diving into Angel Fire come this December!</span>
  <a data-text-id="144754949496129354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_146252763" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146252763" />
    <a title="Crystal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250501-crystal"><img alt="Crystal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378941415p2/2250501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146252763?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal" href="/user/show/2250501-crystal">Crystal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250501-crystal?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146252763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13529463183128949643">This review is somewhat spoilerish be warned..<br/><br/>I am so confused with how I feel about this book. I liked it, but there are just a few things that I am not comfortable/used to and that makes it hard for me. I went with a 4 star because the concept is very original and I have to give the author major props for looking outside the box.<br/>Story first, Willow is not your ordinary girl. First of all she is a mechanic and no I am not being sexist I just haven't read many books where the heroine works on ca</span>
  <span id="freeText13529463183128949643" style="display:none">This review is somewhat spoilerish be warned..<br /><br />I am so confused with how I feel about this book. I liked it, but there are just a few things that I am not comfortable/used to and that makes it hard for me. I went with a 4 star because the concept is very original and I have to give the author major props for looking outside the box.<br />Story first, Willow is not your ordinary girl. First of all she is a mechanic and no I am not being sexist I just haven't read many books where the heroine works on cars. The author even points out that this makes her stand out in a not so good way at school so my view point is taken directly from the author. Willow is also a psychic. She can read peoples future by simply taking their hands. The combination of these two things make Willow stand out as "weird" among her peers. When she agrees to do a reading for Beth, the most perfect and popular girl at school, Willow sees a man who says he is Beths angel and even though Beth thinks this man is her divine intervention, Willow suspects different. Beth ends up taking the path that Willow begs her not too, thus throwing Willow into a whole new world the Church of Angels. This community is more than what it seems and Willow finds out that Angels are not the pretty picture she was brought up to believe. Alex on the other hand has grown up knowing exactly what angels are capable of. He is known as an AK, angel killer. He was brought up at a camp run by his father training to become an AK and save the world. When certain events happen the CIA steps in and makes it mandatory that all AK's live and hunt alone. So for two years Alex just waits in hotels until he gets his next assignment. He is by far the best so when he gets a text telling him to go to Willows house and terminate the problem he goes without question. When he arrives at her house and realizes that Willow is not his regular target he starts to wonder why the CIA wants her dead. What follows changes both their lives and they learn that angels are not always what they seem.<br />That is the basic story and I enjoyed it I just don't know how I feel about Weatherly turning angels into life sucking fiends. I have learned when reading you have to suspend your reality and I can typically do that but with this one the reality just felt uncomfortable for some reason. I think given enough time and with the second book I will be able to buy this concept but right now I am just lost because I really liked the story. I even liked the angel burn effect that the author created. It made total sense and was very unique in my opinion. <br />My other problem was that the climax of the story sorta fell flat. I was really into it and then boom nothing. The story focused more on the will Alex get to Willow in time instead of will this plan actually work and save the day. I wanted more. That being said though I really liked the relationship between Alex and Willow. Yes, they love each other and it is that all consuming love, but I have come to realize that if I was in that situation and I spent every night and day with a hawt guy who took care of me and saved my life I would probably develop strong feeling for that said person. I get the who I love you stuff now in YA books. Think back to when you were a teenager, most girls and guys loved each other after the second week without all the intense situations that the teens in books are in. So I am getting off my soapbox and I am just going to say that I totally bought the romance and I loved every minute of it.<br />I think fans of YA will adore this book and I have a feeling that my problems with the angel concept are just my own. I am looking forward to the sequel.<br /><br />Thank you Candlewick Press and Netgalley for the opportunity to read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13529463183128949643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_124965551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124965551" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124965551?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763656522" href="/book/show/9713071-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124965551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7614673813654892975">I think I prefer the UK cover to the US one but they both have their positives, I guess.<br/><br/>I’m a bit wary of angel books because they can either be exceptionally good, <i>Unearthly</i>, or absolutely terrible, <i>Hush, Hush</i>. <i>Angel Burn</i> falls somewhere in the middle; nothing offensive but doesn’t evolve past being anything more than pleasant. <br/><br/>There’s a lot of good things to say about this book though. Willow being savvy at fixing cars? Fantastic! And the whole angel mythology doesn’t revolve around heaven, Je</span>
  <span id="freeText7614673813654892975" style="display:none">I think I prefer the UK cover to the US one but they both have their positives, I guess.<br /><br />I’m a bit wary of angel books because they can either be exceptionally good, <i>Unearthly</i>, or absolutely terrible, <i>Hush, Hush</i>. <i>Angel Burn</i> falls somewhere in the middle; nothing offensive but doesn’t evolve past being anything more than pleasant. <br /><br />There’s a lot of good things to say about this book though. Willow being savvy at fixing cars? Fantastic! And the whole angel mythology doesn’t revolve around heaven, Jesus, and all that stuff? Great! (I don’t have a problem with this stuff, just to be clear) The angels here are more like incubi/succubi from another realm come to prey on humans. I thought this was a new and refreshing take on them versus the overdone fallen angel or angel on a mission angle. <br /><br />This book is one of those fun chase, adventure, and escape book with a slight touch of saving the word thrown in there. So if you’re tired of the whole high school drama angst-fest than have no fear, this is not what’s going on in here. The romance wasn’t that bad either. The guy, Alex, is not a prick and there is no dreaded love triangle in here.<br /><br />At first I was really a fan of the romance because they were both awkward and bumbling around each other. They were both insecure and tentative as they worked toward their gradual relationship. But then once they got together there were oh so sappy. It made me want to gag. It didn’t help that they spent chapters hiding out in a cabin in the woods so all they did was profess overly saccharine sentiments to each other and on and on.<br /><br />The whole race across the US felt a bit, I don’t know, flat after a while. I got tired of them just stopping over at random places and changing cars. The scenery and pacing was the same so, yeah, I wanted something more fun. But it did keep the pace up, so while I didn’t like it, I’m quite sure a lot of other people would love this part.<br /><br />The writing reminded me of an adventure book. Very plain and straight to the point without much frilly descriptions. The majority of the book consisted of pov changes between Alex and Willow, which were actually done pretty well. When they switched over, the transition was seamless and not jarring at all. The book ended on a high note and wrapped all the loose threads so well, I have no idea how the sequel will be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7614673813654892975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_534520430" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/534520430" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/534520430?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763656522" href="/book/show/9713071-angel-burn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=angels">angels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer534520430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3524275884054314846"><a href='http://www.flickr.com/photos/67647245@N07/9443636588/' title='14r4i_zps2fc66efc by tina Ceballos, on Flickr' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409403i/801626.jpg' width='480' height='319' alt='14r4i_zps2fc66efc' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>2.5 STARS</i>
</b><br/><br/>Though truth be told, coming in, I did have some high expectations seeing as I've read the better angel books ahead of reading this.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Angel Burn</b>
</i> has quite the interesting twist in the angels sub-genre in that instead of having the usual religious backstory, angels are featured as beautiful, alien-like beings who come from a dying world and has come to our own using humans as sort of energy sources much like parasites. Shades of The Matrix' mythology now that I think about it. </span>
  <span id="freeText3524275884054314846" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/67647245@N07/9443636588/" title="14r4i_zps2fc66efc by tina Ceballos, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409403i/801626.jpg" width="480" height="319" alt="14r4i_zps2fc66efc" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>2.5 STARS</i>
</b><br><br>Though truth be told, coming in, I did have some high expectations seeing as I've read the better angel books ahead of reading this.<br><br><i>
  <b>Angel Burn</b>
</i> has quite the interesting twist in the angels sub-genre in that instead of having the usual religious backstory, angels are featured as beautiful, alien-like beings who come from a dying world and has come to our own using humans as sort of energy sources much like parasites. Shades of The Matrix' mythology now that I think about it. The title actually pertains to the residual effects of the angels feeding off humans that leads to blind angel adoration. What I found wholly fascinating about this story was how I realized that the scenario presented by this book is pretty realistic. In that in the event that angels make themselves known to us (wings and halo and all), knowing human behavior, forming a cult-like organization centered on them is not a too far off possibility. <br><br>The story kicks off when our heroine, Willow Fields, your typical high school girl who just happens to also have amazing psychic abilities, had to do a reading on popular girl Beth. Now Beth has been "touched by an angel" so to speak and seeks Willow's help in making a decision to leave her life and join the Church of Angels. When Willow warns Beth of the truth behind this "encounter" her life is placed in danger while she becomes fully aware on what her abilities are borne from.<br><br>This had all the right ingredients: a strong heroine, the hero is an Angel Killer who spent half the time in the book shirtless (!), a road trip set in the desert (!!) and a solid story setting to back it all up. But somehow the end product felt this side of bland.<br><br>The writing was okay but didn't hook my attention enough to keep my wandering thoughts away from nitpicking.There's a certain lack of emotional panache in this story. I do not seek all-out DRAMA especially in YA books but that subtle tug was sorely missed here. The characters were likable enough -- I liked Willow's quirk of being a car geek and a "skirt mechanic" so to speak and Alex' past of growing up in an Angel Killer camp, with a Sears catalog as his source of education was interesting. But somehow, the story failed to capitalize on these aspects to give them better chemistry with each other. I wish the author exploited these avenues (and my feels) better to make them beyond likable, because I feel like I could've <i>
  <b>cried</b>
</i> for the right reasons at the right moments for these two. <br><br>But I just ended up crying in frustration.<br><br>Willow's character felt a bit small against the enormity of her role in the grand scheme of things. Even the circumstances surrounding her joining Alex didn't feel logically sound. Her powers <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ as a half-angel <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> seriously needed some limits because at times, I had to question what was the point of Alex taking her away from everyone when she had all these abilities. I'm also not a fan of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the angel and human parts of Willow being separate entities  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, why can't they just be one and the same? It gets a bit confusing in the narrative.<br><br>Alex was a good hero but again, could've used a bit of drama on his past. He would've been a more interesting hero for me if <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he had to kill his brother himself after falling victim to Angel Burn than his actual story of guilt over watching an angel kill his brother in front of him <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br>On the other side of the fence, the evil mastermind Raziel felt underdeveloped while the nameless angels pursuing Willow and Alex felt cartoonish in their scare factor. It is horrible to think that these angels can <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ give you cancer or MS or a massive stroke with their touch <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but again, this kind of takes away a bit of the dramatic horror I would've wanted to feel some of everyone's urgency and fear.<br><br>I want to nitpick some more but I'm putting away the red sharpie. This really had a good deal of potential but just lacked a bit of push to commit as a PNR. The book focused and failed a great deal on the romance between Alex and Willow but I have a feeling it would've fared better if this aspect of the story was kept to the background and the Angel Invasion was brought to the fore.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3524275884054314846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
